    <meta name="dc.description" content="Sodium-ion batteries have emerged as competitive substitutes for low-temperature applications due to severe capacity loss and safety concerns of lithium-ion batteries at − 20&amp;nbsp;°C or lower. However, the key capability of ultrafast charging at ultralow temperature for SIBs is rarely reported. Herein, a hybrid of Bi nanoparticles embedded in carbon nanorods is demonstrated as an ideal material to address this issue, which is synthesized via a high temperature shock method. Such a hybrid shows an unprecedented rate performance (237.9&amp;nbsp;mAh&amp;nbsp;g−1 at 2&amp;nbsp;A&amp;nbsp;g−1) at − 60&amp;nbsp;°C, outperforming all reported SIB anode materials. Coupled with a Na3V2(PO4)3 cathode, the energy density of the full cell can reach to 181.9 Wh kg−1 at − 40&amp;nbsp;°C. Based on this work, a novel strategy of high-rate activation is proposed to enhance performances of Bi-based materials in cryogenic conditions by creating new active sites for interfacial reaction under large current.">

    <meta property="og:url" content="https://link.springer.com/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9">
    <meta property="og:type" content="article">
    <meta property="og:site_name" content="SpringerLink">
    <meta property="og:title" content="Ideal Bi-Based Hybrid Anode Material for Ultrafast Charging of Sodium-Ion Batteries at Extremely Low Temperatures - Nano-Micro Letters">
    <meta property="og:description" content="Sodium-ion batteries have emerged as competitive substitutes for low-temperature applications due to severe capacity loss and safety concerns of lithium-ion batteries at − 20 °C or lower. However, the key capability of ultrafast charging at ultralow temperature for SIBs is rarely reported. Herein, a hybrid of Bi nanoparticles embedded in carbon nanorods is demonstrated as an ideal material to address this issue, which is synthesized via a high temperature shock method. Such a hybrid shows an unprecedented rate performance (237.9 mAh g−1 at 2 A g−1) at − 60 °C, outperforming all reported SIB anode materials. Coupled with a Na3V2(PO4)3 cathode, the energy density of the full cell can reach to 181.9 Wh kg−1 at − 40 °C. Based on this work, a novel strategy of high-rate activation is proposed to enhance performances of Bi-based materials in cryogenic conditions by creating new active sites for interfacial reaction under large current.">
    <meta property="og:image" content="https://static-content.springer.com/image/art%3A10.1007%2Fs40820-024-01560-9/MediaObjects/40820_2024_1560_Figa_HTML.png">

    <script type="application/ld+json">{"mainEntity":{"headline":"Ideal Bi-Based Hybrid Anode Material for Ultrafast Charging of Sodium-Ion Batteries at Extremely Low Temperatures","description":"\n\n                \n                  \n                \n                \n                  \n                \n                \n                  \n                \n               Sodium-ion batteries have emerged as competitive substitutes for low-temperature applications due to severe capacity loss and safety concerns of lithium-ion batteries at − 20 °C or lower. However, the key capability of ultrafast charging at ultralow temperature for SIBs is rarely reported. Herein, a hybrid of Bi nanoparticles embedded in carbon nanorods is demonstrated as an ideal material to address this issue, which is synthesized via a high temperature shock method. Such a hybrid shows an unprecedented rate performance (237.9 mAh g−1 at 2 A g−1) at − 60 °C, outperforming all reported SIB anode materials. Coupled with a Na3V2(PO4)3 cathode, the energy density of the full cell can reach to 181.9 Wh kg−1 at − 40 °C. Based on this work, a novel strategy of high-rate activation is proposed to enhance performances of Bi-based materials in cryogenic conditions by creating new active sites for interfacial reaction under large current. \n\n                \n                  \n                \n                 <div data-article-body="true" data-track-component="article body" class="c-article-body">
                    
                    <section aria-labelledby="Abs123" data-title="Highlights" lang="en"><div class="c-article-section" id="Abs123-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Abs123">Highlights</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Abs123-content">
              
              
<ul class="u-list-style-bullet">
                <li>
                  <p>Metallic nanoparticles with excellent size controllability and high loading rate are obtained via ultrafast high temperature shock method.</p>
                </li>
                <li>
                  <p>The Bi/CNRs-15 electrode exhibits an unprecedented rate performance (237.9&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 2&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>) at − 60&nbsp;°C, while the energy density of the full cell can reach to 181.9&nbsp;Wh&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup> at − 40&nbsp;°C.</p>
                </li>
                <li>
                  <p>A novel strategy of high-rate activation is proposed to obtain high capacity and superior stability at low temperature by creating new active sites for interfacial reaction.</p>
                </li>
              </ul>
            </div></div></section><section aria-labelledby="Abs2" data-title="Abstract" lang="en"><div class="c-article-section" id="Abs2-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Abs2">Abstract</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Abs2-content"><p>Sodium-ion batteries have emerged as competitive substitutes for low-temperature applications due to severe capacity loss and safety concerns of lithium-ion batteries at − 20&nbsp;°C or lower. However, the key capability of ultrafast charging at ultralow temperature for SIBs is rarely reported. Herein, a hybrid of Bi nanoparticles embedded in carbon nanorods is demonstrated as an ideal material to address this issue, which is synthesized via a high temperature shock method. Such a hybrid shows an unprecedented rate performance (237.9&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 2&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>) at − 60&nbsp;°C, outperforming all reported SIB anode materials. Coupled with a Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> cathode, the energy density of the full cell can reach to 181.9 Wh kg<sup>−1</sup> at − 40&nbsp;°C. Based on this work, a novel strategy of high-rate activation is proposed to enhance performances of Bi-based materials in cryogenic conditions by creating new active sites for interfacial reaction under large current.</p>
<div class="c-article-section__figure" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure"><figure><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><picture><source type="image/webp" srcset="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1007%2Fs40820-024-01560-9/MediaObjects/40820_2024_1560_Figa_HTML.png?as=webp"><img src="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1007%2Fs40820-024-01560-9/MediaObjects/40820_2024_1560_Figa_HTML.png" alt="" loading="lazy" width="685" height="443"></picture></div></div></figure></div></div></div></section>

                                <div class="main-content">
                                    <section data-title="Introduction"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec2-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec2"><span class="c-article-section__title-number">1 </span>Introduction</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec2-content"><p>Lithium-ion batteries (LIBs) have accounted for a dominant position in energy storage fields from portable electronic equipment to electric vehicles (EVs) thanks to their high energy density and long lifespan [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="H. Jin, S. Xin, C. Chuang, W. Li, H. Wang et al., Black phosphorus composites with engineered interfaces for high-rate high-capacity lithium storage. Science 370, 192–197 (2020). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1126/science.aav5842
                  
                " href="#ref-CR1" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e442">1</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="R.A. House, U. Maitra, M.A. Pérez-Osorio, J.G. Lozano, L. Jin et al., Superstructure control of first-cycle voltage hysteresis in oxygen-redox cathodes. Nature 577, 502–508 (2020). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1038/s41586-019-1854-3
                  
                " href="#ref-CR2" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e442_1">2</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 3" title="D. Lu, R. Li, M.M. Rahman, P. Yu, L. Lv et al., Ligand-channel-enabled ultrafast Li-ion conduction. Nature 627, 101–107 (2024). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1038/s41586-024-07045-4
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR3" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e445">3</a>]. However, severe ionic conductivity decline, sluggish interfacial charge transfer kinetics, fatal dendrite formation and fragile electrolyte/electrode interphase may all deal a crushing blow to the battery performances and safety concerns at subzero temperature, seriously restricting practical applications at high latitudes or altitudes localities, and the fields of civil and military [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="M. Armand, J.-M. Tarascon, Building better batteries. Nature 451, 652–657 (2008). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1038/451652a
                  
                " href="#ref-CR4" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e448">4</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="A. Gupta, A. Manthiram, Designing advanced lithium-based batteries for low-temperature conditions. Adv. Energy Mater. 10, 2001972 (2020). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/aenm.202001972
                  
                " href="#ref-CR5" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e448_1">5</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 6" title="N. Zhang, T. Deng, S. Zhang, C. Wang, L. Chen et al., Critical review on low-temperature Li-ion/metal batteries. Adv. Mater. 34, e2107899 (2022). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/adma.202107899
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR6" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e451">6</a>]. As a consequence, developing advanced energy storage devices with superior temperature tolerance, which could accommodate to the harsh working conditions brought by diverse seasons and regions, is highly desirable. Sodium-ion batteries (SIBs) have gained extensive concerns owing to wide distribution, cost-effectiveness and natural abundance of sodium resources [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="J.-L. Xia, D. Yan, L.-P. Guo, X.-L. Dong, W.-C. Li et al., Hard carbon nanosheets with uniform ultramicropores and accessible functional groups showing high realistic capacity and superior rate performance for sodium-ion storage. Adv. Mater. 32, e2000447 (2020). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/adma.202000447
                  
                " href="#ref-CR7" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e454">7</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="K.H. Shin, S.K. Park, P. Nakhanivej, Y. Wang, P. Liu et al., Biomimetic composite architecture achieves ultrahigh rate capability and cycling life of sodium ion battery cathodes. Appl. Phys. Rev. 7, 041410 (2020). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1063/5.0020805
                  
                " href="#ref-CR8" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e454_1">8</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="M. Wu, J. Liao, L. Yu, R. Lv, P. Li et al., 2020 roadmap on carbon materials for energy storage and conversion. Chem 15, 995–1013 (2020). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/asia.201901802
                  
                " href="#ref-CR9" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e454_2">9</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 10" title="Z. Song, G. Zhang, X. Deng, Y. Tian, X. Xiao et al., Strongly coupled interfacial engineering inspired by robotic arms enable high-performance sodium-ion capacitors. Adv. Funct. Mater. 32, 2205453 (2022). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/adfm.202205453
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR10" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e458">10</a>]. Additionally, Na<sup>+</sup> has smaller de-solvation energy compared with Li<sup>+</sup>, demonstrating a lower activation barrier for Na<sup>+</sup> insertion/extraction and thus better electrochemical performances at low temperature [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="T. Hosaka, K. Kubota, A.S. Hameed, S. Komaba, Research development on K-ion batteries. Chem. Rev. 120, 6358–6466 (2020). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1021/acs.chemrev.9b00463
                  
                " href="#ref-CR11" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e467">11</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="W. Zhang, X. Sun, Y. Tang, H. Xia, Y. Zeng et al., Lowering charge transfer barrier of LiMn2O4 via nickel surface doping to enhance Li+ intercalation kinetics at subzero temperatures. J. Am. Chem. Soc. 141, 14038–14042 (2019). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1021/jacs.9b05531
                  
                " href="#ref-CR12" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e467_1">12</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 13" title="X. Deng, K. Zou, R. Momen, P. Cai, J. Chen et al., High content anion (S/Se/P) doping assisted by defect engineering with fast charge transfer kinetics for high-performance sodium ion capacitors. Sci. Bull. 66, 1858–1868 (2021). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.scib.2021.04.042
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR13" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e470">13</a>]. Nonetheless, the low operating temperature, especially at high charging rates, could bring decreased ionic conductivity due to increased electrolyte viscosity and unstable interfacial reaction, resulting in severe polarization and capacity decay [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 14" title="J. Qin, Q. Lan, N. Liu, Y. Zhao, Z. Song et al., A metal-free battery working at −80&nbsp;°C. Energy Storage Mater. 26, 585–592 (2020). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.ensm.2019.12.002
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR14" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e474">14</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 15" title="X. Gao, X. Du, T.S. Mathis, M. Zhang, X. Wang et al., Maximizing ion accessibility in MXene-knotted carbon nanotube composite electrodes for high-rate electrochemical energy storage. Nat. Commun. 11, 6160 (2020). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1038/s41467-020-19992-3
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR15" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e477">15</a>]. So far, the studies of low-temperature SIBs principally focus on modulating the solvation structure and developing electrolytes with low freezing point, which is far from sufficient, let alone the ultrafast charging capability at ultralow temperature [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="S. Yuan, T. Kong, Y. Zhang, P. Dong, Y. Zhang et al., Advanced electrolyte design for high-energy-density Li-metal batteries under practical conditions. Angew. Chem. Int. Ed. 60, 25624–25638 (2021). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/anie.202108397
                  
                " href="#ref-CR16" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e480">16</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="S. Zhong, Y. Yu, Y. Yang, Y. Yao, L. Wang et al., Molecular engineering on solvation structure of carbonate electrolyte toward durable sodium metal battery at −40&nbsp;°C. Angew. Chem. Int. Ed. 62, e202301169 (2023). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/anie.202301169
                  
                " href="#ref-CR17" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e480_1">17</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 18" title="C. Yang, X. Liu, Y. Lin, L. Yin, J. Lu et al., Entropy-driven solvation toward low-temperature sodium-ion batteries with temperature-adaptive feature. Adv. Mater. 35, e2301817 (2023). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/adma.202301817
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR18" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e483">18</a>]. In order to promote practical applications of SIBs in cryogenic environments, it is also crucial to enhance the electrode electrochemical performance through structural modification, coating and other strategies [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 19" title="H. Yuan, F. Ma, X. Wei, J.-L. Lan, Y. Liu et al., Solid electrolyte interphases: ionic-conducting and robust multilayered solid electrolyte interphases for greatly improved rate and cycling capabilities of sodium ion full cells (adv. energy mater. 37/2020). Adv. Energy Mater. 10, 2070153 (2020). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/aenm.202070153
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR19" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e486">19</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 20" title="X. Qi, H. Dong, H. Yan, B. Hou, H. Liu et al., Hollow core-shelled Na4Fe2.4Ni0.6(PO4)2P2O7 with tiny-void space capable fast-charge and low-temperature sodium storage. Angew. Chem. Int. 63, e202410590 (2024). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/anie.202410590
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR20" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e489">20</a>].</p><p>Alloy-type materials, featuring relatively low redox reaction potential and high energy density, have been considered to be promising anode candidates for SIBs [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="X. Cheng, Y. Sun, D. Li, H. Yang, F. Chen et al., From 0D to 3D: dimensional control of bismuth for potassium storage with superb kinetics and cycling stability. Adv. Energy Mater. 11, 2102263 (2021). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/aenm.202102263
                  
                " href="#ref-CR21" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e495">21</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="R.C. Cui, H.Y. Zhou, J.C. Li, C.C. Yang, Q. Jiang, Ball-Cactus-like Bi embedded in N-riched carbon nanonetworks enables the best potassium storage performance. Adv. Funct. Mater. 31, 2103067 (2021). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/adfm.202103067
                  
                " href="#ref-CR22" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e495_1">22</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 23" title="S.-L. Wei, Y.-L. Yang, J.-G. Chen, X.-L. Shi, Y. Sun et al., A fast-charging and ultra-stable sodium-ion battery anode enabled by N-doped Bi/BiOCl in a carbon framework. Adv. Energy Mater. (2024). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/aenm.202401825
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR23" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e498">23</a>]. Among them, Bi with large lattice spacing [d<sub>(003)</sub> = 3.95&nbsp;Å], high electronic conductivity (7.8 × 10<sup>5</sup>&nbsp;S&nbsp;m<sup>−1</sup>) and theoretical capacity (385&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>), has attracted great attentions [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 24" title="C. Wang, D. Du, M. Song, Y. Wang, F. Li, A high-power Na3V2(PO4)3-Bi sodium-ion full battery in a wide temperature range. Adv. Energy Mater. 9, 1900022 (2019). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/aenm.201900022
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR24" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e510">24</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 25" title="C. Wang, L. Wang, F. Li, F. Cheng, J. Chen, Bulk bismuth as a high-capacity and ultralong cycle-life anode for sodium-ion batteries by coupling with glyme-based electrolytes. Adv. Mater. 29, 1702212 (2017). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/adma.201702212
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR25" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e513">25</a>]. Wang and coworkers reported that the pure Bi electrode combined with ether-based electrolytes exhibited prospective low-temperature behavior (370&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.02&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at − 40&nbsp;°C) owing to the solvent co-intercalation process [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 26" title="Z. Li, Y. Zhang, J. Zhang, Y. Cao, J. Chen et al., Sodium-ion battery with a wide operation-temperature range from-70 to 100 °C. Angew. Chem. Int. Ed. 61, e202116930 (2022). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/anie.202116930
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR26" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e520">26</a>]. Notwithstanding, the cycling stability and rate performance are still limited at ultralow temperature [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 27" title="L. Liu, S. Li, L. Hu, X. Liang, W. Yang et al., Bi@C nanosphere anode with Na+-ether-solvent cointercalation behavior to achieve fast sodium storage under extreme low temperatures. Carbon Energy 6, e531 (2024). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/cey2.531
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e524">27</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 28" title="Y. Wang, X. Xu, Y. Wu, F. Li, W. Fan et al., Facile galvanic replacement construction of Bi@C nanosheets array as binder-free anodes for superior sodium-ion batteries. Adv. Energy Mater. 14, 2401833 (2024). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/aenm.202401833
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR28" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e527">28</a>]. Batteries with extremely fast charging capability and long life spans are highly expected on account of the demands for high-power EVs and tools in cold region [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 29" title="Y. Zhang, W. Zhao, C. Kang, S. Geng, J. Zhu et al., Phase-junction engineering triggered built-in electric field for fast-charging batteries operated at −30&nbsp;°C. Matter 6, 1928–1944 (2023). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.matt.2023.03.026
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR29" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e530">29</a>]. It has been proved that designing unique nanostructures is an effective strategy to improve the rate property and cyclability [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 6" title="N. Zhang, T. Deng, S. Zhang, C. Wang, L. Chen et al., Critical review on low-temperature Li-ion/metal batteries. Adv. Mater. 34, e2107899 (2022). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/adma.202107899
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR6" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e533">6</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 30" title="J. Xu, H. Zhang, F. Yu, Y. Cao, M. Liao et al., Realizing all-climate Li-S batteries by using a porous sub-nano aromatic framework. Angew. Chem. Int. Ed. 61, e202211933 (2022). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/anie.202211933
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR30" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e536">30</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 31" title="S. Xin, Y. You, S. Wang, H.-C. Gao, Y.-X. Yin et al., Solid-state lithium metal batteries promoted by nanotechnology: progress and prospects. ACS Energy Lett. 2, 1385–1394 (2017). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1021/acsenergylett.7b00175
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR31" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e539">31</a>]. Thermal treatment is frequently used to fabricate nanomaterials from metal salt precursors. However, the conventional methods based on tube furnace annealing (TFA) generally require relatively long synthesis duration and suffer from low energy utilization efficiency [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 32" title="M. Guo, Q. Dong, H. Xie, C. Wang, Y. Zhao et al., Ultrafast high-temperature sintering to avoid metal loss toward high-performance and scalable cermets. Matter 5, 594–604 (2022). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.matt.2021.11.008
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR32" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e543">32</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 33" title="M. Cui, C. Yang, S. Hwang, B. Li, Q. Dong et al., Rapid atomic ordering transformation toward intermetallic nanoparticles. Nano Lett. 22, 255–262 (2022). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1021/acs.nanolett.1c03714
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR33" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e546">33</a>]. Uneven heating conditions also give rise to nanoparticle aggregation. Therefore, a rapid and highly effective method for the synthesis of electrode materials is still in high demand. High temperature shock (HTS), a facile and ultrafast synthesis method, has been utilized not only in domains like catalysis, but also in the fabrication of battery electrode materials in recent years [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="T. Jiang, Z. Liu, Y. Yuan, X. Zheng, S. Park et al., Ultrafast electrical pulse synthesis of highly active electrocatalysts for beyond-industrial-level hydrogen gas batteries. Adv. Mater. 35, e2300502 (2023). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/adma.202300502
                  
                " href="#ref-CR34" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e549">34</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="S. Liu, Y. Shen, Y. Zhang, B. Cui, S. Xi et al., Extreme environmental thermal shock induced dislocation-rich Pt nanoparticles boosting hydrogen evolution reaction. Adv. Mater. 34, e2106973 (2022). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/adma.202106973
                  
                " href="#ref-CR35" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e549_1">35</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="S. Dou, J. Xu, D. Zhang, W. Liu, C. Zeng et al., Ultrarapid nanomanufacturing of high-quality bimetallic anode library toward stable potassium-ion storage. Angew. Chem. Int. Ed. 62, e202303600 (2023). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/anie.202303600
                  
                " href="#ref-CR36" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e549_2">36</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 37" title="X. Wu, Z. Li, W. Feng, W. Luo, L. Liao et al., Insights into electrolyte-induced temporal and spatial evolution of an ultrafast-charging bi-based anode for sodium-ion batteries. Energy Storage Mater. 66, 103219 (2024). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.ensm.2024.103219
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR37" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e552">37</a>].</p><p>Herein, a hybrid of well-dispersed and high-loading Bi nanoparticles embedded in carbon nanorods is fabricated by ultrafast HTS for only 15&nbsp;s (Bi/CNRs-15), which is demonstrated as an ideal material for ultralow-temperature ultrafast-charging SIBs. The instantaneously generated high temperature can effectively decompose the precursors of metal–organic frameworks (MOFs) to metallic Bi nanoparticles with excellent size controllability and high loading rate. The fast heating and cooling rates inhibit the aggregation of nanoparticles, which considerably shortens the ions/electrons diffusion path. As expected, the designed Bi/CNRs-15 anode displays incredible temperature tolerance, fast charging capability (261.4&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at a high rate of 5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>) and cycling stability (241.7&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 2400 cycles) at − 40&nbsp;°C. Even at an extremely low temperature of − 60&nbsp;°C, the hybrid also delivers a high capacity of 237.9&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 2&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, surpassing all reported SIB anode materials. Furthermore, a stable and homogenous solid-electrolyte interface (SEI) layer with more inorganic species could improve structural stability and boost rate kinetics in some degree, which is unraveled by X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy etching. Moreover, it is worth noting that an unusual phenomenon of capacity increment named “negative fading” takes place after high-rate cycling under low-temperature conditions, which provides a new route to enhance the low-temperature performances of SIBs.</p></div></div></section><section data-title="Experimental Section"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec3-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec3"><span class="c-article-section__title-number">2 </span>Experimental Section</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec3-content"><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec4"><span class="c-article-section__title-number">2.1 </span>Materials</h3><p>All chemicals of bismuth chloride (BiCl<sub>3</sub>, 99%, Macklin Reagent Co., Ltd.), potassium iodide (KI, 99%, Aladdin Reagent Co., Ltd.), acetic acid (CH<sub>3</sub>COOH, 99.5%, Macklin Reagent Co., Ltd.), trimesic acid (H<sub>3</sub>BTC, 99.9%, Aladdin Reagent Co., Ltd.), methanol (CH<sub>3</sub>OH, 99%, Beijing Chemical Works) and dimethylformamide (DMF, 99%, Aladdin Reagent Co., Ltd.) were used without further purification. The ultrapure water used in all experiments was with a specific resistance of 18.2&nbsp;MΩ&nbsp;cm.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec5"><span class="c-article-section__title-number">2.2 </span>Preparation of Bi/CNRs-15</h3><p>First, Bi-MOFs were synthesized via a modified two-step solvothermal method. Typically, BiCl<sub>3</sub> (0.5&nbsp;mmol) and KI (0.5&nbsp;mmol) were dispersed in acetic acid (50&nbsp;mL) and deionized (DI) water (12.5&nbsp;mL), respectively. After fully stirred, these two solutions were mixed to form the tender green suspension and the pH value of the mixture was adjusted to 6. After 30&nbsp;min of stirring, the above dispersion was transferred into a Polytetrafluoroethylene lined stainless steel autoclave and kept at 160&nbsp;°C for 2&nbsp;h. Then BiOI nanosheets (BiOI NSs) were obtained after centrifugation and freeze drying. Subsequently, BiOI NSs (0.5&nbsp;g) and H<sub>3</sub>BTC (0.9&nbsp;g) were dissolved in the mixture of dimethylformamide (22.5&nbsp;mL) and methanol (7.5&nbsp;mL) and magnetically stirred for 30&nbsp;min. Thereafter, the obtained solution was shifted to a 50&nbsp;mL Teflon-lined autoclave and held at 120&nbsp;°C for 3&nbsp;h. The powders of Bi-MOFs were assembled by filtration, washing and drying. Finally, the carbon cloth loaded with Bi-MOFs was clipped into copper electrodes of DC power to acquire Bi/CNRs-15, which was passed a current of 10 A in the argon-filled glovebox for 15&nbsp;s. Besides, contrast samples shocked for 5 and 30&nbsp;s were also synthesized, which are denoted as Bi/CNRs-5 and Bi/CNRs-30, respectively. As a comparison, Bi/CNRs-TFA was synthesized by a conventional TFA treatment. The same Bi-MOF precursors were placed in a tube furnace annealed at 600&nbsp;°C for 2&nbsp;h in an Ar/H<sub>2</sub> (with 5 vol% H<sub>2</sub>) atmosphere.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec6"><span class="c-article-section__title-number">2.3 </span>Materials Characterization</h3><p>X-ray diffraction (XRD) analysis was performed on an instrument with Cu Kα (Rigaku D/Max-2550). Transmission electron microscopy (TEM, JEM-2100F, JEOL) and field-emission scanning electron microscopy (FESEM, JSM-6700F, JEOL) were fulfilled to obtain the structure and morphology of all samples. Raman spectra were carried out by a micro-Raman spectrometer (Renishaw). X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy (XPS) data were collected at an ESCALAB 250Xi system. Thermogravimetric analysis (TGA) was performed in the air using an SDT Q600 instrument. The nitrogen adsorption and desorption (Micromeritics ASAP 2020 analyzer) was used to test the specific surface area and pore sizes. The carbon vacancies were measured by the electron paramagnetic resonance (EPR) technique on a Bruker EMX plusmachine. <i>In-situ</i> XRD was performed on a Rigaku Smart lab. Low-temperature electrochemical tests were conducted in the high and low temperature test chamber (BPH-060).</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec7"><span class="c-article-section__title-number">2.4 </span>Electrochemical Measurements</h3><p>All CR2025-type coin cells were assembled in an argon-filled glove box by employing Na metal as the counter electrode, Whatman glass fiber (GF/C) as the separator, and 1&nbsp;M NaPF<sub>6</sub> in 1,2-dimethoxyethane (DME) as the electrolyte. The active materials (Bi/CNRs-15, Bi/CNRs-5, Bi/CNRs-30, Bi/CNRs-TFA, pure Bi) were mixed with Super P and sodium carboxymethylcellulose with a weight ratio of 7:2:1. The mixed slurry was uniformly pasted on Cu foil and dried in a vacuum oven at 70&nbsp;°C. Additionally, the mass loadings of active materials were ranging from 0.6 to 4.2&nbsp;mg&nbsp;cm<sup>−2</sup>. In this work, all capacities are evaluated by the whole weight of the Bi/CNRs-15 composite. The electrodes were tested 3 cycles at 1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at room temperature before transferring to the high and low temperature test chamber. The cathode consists of Na<sub>3</sub>V<sub>2</sub>(PO<sub>4</sub>)<sub>3</sub> (NVP), Super P and polyvinylidene fluoride in a mass ratio of 7:2:1. The full cell was assembled using NVP and Bi/CNRs-15 as the cathode and anode, respectively, with the same electrolyte and separator. Meanwhile, the voltage range was selected at 1.5–3.3&nbsp;V for the full cell, and the anode was electrochemically activated for 3 cycles before it was used in the full cell. The galvanostatic charge/discharge and GITT tests were implemented using a LAND-CT2001A battery testing system in 0.01–1.5&nbsp;V (<i>vs.</i> Na<sup>+</sup>/Na) at room temperature/low temperature. The pulse current, duration and relaxation time of the GITT tests are 50&nbsp;mA&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, 600&nbsp;s, and 3600&nbsp;s, respectively. CV curves and temperature-dependent EIS measurements with a frequency range of 100&nbsp;kHz to 0.01&nbsp;Hz were performed on an electrochemical workstation (Ivium-n-Stat).</p></div></div></section><section data-title="Results and Discussion"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec8-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec8"><span class="c-article-section__title-number">3 </span>Results and Discussion</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec8-content"><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec9"><span class="c-article-section__title-number">3.1 </span>Synthesis and Characterization</h3><p>The synthesis route of Bi/CNRs-15 is schematically illustrated in Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#Fig1">1</a>a. It has been reported that MOF-based materials present vast opportunities in the quest for optimal electrode materials for rechargeable batteries due to their high porosity, diverse structures and controllable chemical compositions [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="L. Zhang, Y. Hou, The Rise and development of MOF-based materials for metal-chalcogen batteries: current status, challenges, and prospects. Adv. Energy Mater. 13, 2204378 (2023). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/aenm.202204378
                  
                " href="#ref-CR38" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e664">38</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="S.H. Yang, S.K. Park, Y.C. Kang, MOF-derived CoSe2@N-doped carbon matrix confined in hollow mesoporous carbon nanospheres as high-performance anodes for potassium-ion batteries. Nano-Micro Lett. 13, 9 (2020). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1007/s40820-020-00539-6
                  
                " href="#ref-CR39" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e664_1">39</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 40" title="Z.-L. Zheng, M.-M. Wu, X. Zeng, X.-W. Zhu, D. Luo et al., Facile fabrication of hollow nanoporous carbon architectures by controlling MOF crystalline inhomogeneity for ultra-stable Na-ion storage. Angew. Chem. Int. Ed. 63, e202400012 (2024). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/anie.202400012
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR40" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e667">40</a>]. Here, firstly, a Bi-MOF as the precursor (Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#MOESM1">S1</a>) was prepared by a modified two-step solvothermal reaction [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 41" title="D. Yao, C. Tang, A. Vasileff, X. Zhi, Y. Jiao et al., The controllable reconstruction of Bi-MOFs for electrochemical CO2 reduction through electrolyte and potential mediation. Angew. Chem. Int. Ed. 60, 18178–18184 (2021). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/anie.202104747
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR41" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e673">41</a>], in which bismuth chloride (BiCl<sub>3</sub>) as Bi precursor, and the ligand of trimesic acid (H<sub>3</sub>BTC) served as a structure-directing agent and carbon source [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 42" title="J. Liu, Z. Wang, P. Cheng, M.J. Zaworotko, Y. Chen et al., Post-synthetic modifications of metal–organic cages. Nat. Rev. Chem. 6, 339–356 (2022). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1038/s41570-022-00380-y
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR42" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e681">42</a>]. Specifically, the carboxyl group (–COOH) of H<sub>3</sub>BTC lost its proton (H<sup>+</sup>) to form the carboxylate ion (–COO<sup>−</sup>) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 43" title="Z. Wang, Z. Zeng, H. Wang, G. Zeng, P. Xu et al., Bismuth-based metal–organic frameworks and their derivatives: opportunities and challenges. Coord. Chem. Rev. 439, 213902 (2021). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.ccr.2021.213902
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR43" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e691">43</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 44" title="D. Yao, C. Tang, L. Li, B. Xia, A. Vasileff et al., In situ fragmented bismuth nanoparticles for electrocatalytic nitrogen reduction. Adv. Energy Mater. 10, 2001289 (2020). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/aenm.202001289
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR44" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e694">44</a>]. Bi<sup>3+</sup> acted as the central metal ion and coordinated with the -COO<sup>−</sup> of the deprotonated H<sub>3</sub>BTC ligand to form a coordination bond [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 43" title="Z. Wang, Z. Zeng, H. Wang, G. Zeng, P. Xu et al., Bismuth-based metal–organic frameworks and their derivatives: opportunities and challenges. Coord. Chem. Rev. 439, 213902 (2021). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.ccr.2021.213902
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR43" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e703">43</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 45" title="X. Yue, L. Cheng, F. Li, J. Fan, Q. Xiang, Highly strained Bi-MOF on bismuth oxyhalide support with tailored intermediate adsorption/desorption capability for robust CO2 photoreduction. Angew. Chem. Int. Ed. 61, e202208414 (2022). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/anie.202208414
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR45" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e707">45</a>]. After HTS (Fig. S2) in Ar atmosphere for only 15&nbsp;s, the final product of Bi/CNRs-15 was obtained, where Bi nanoparticles were <i>in-situ</i> formed from Bi-MOFs and uniformly embedded in the carbon nanorods. Meanwhile, under the extreme heating generated by HTS, the chlorine can effectively escape from BiOCl (hydrolyzed from BiCl<sub>3</sub>) through the reaction 2BiOCl + C = 2Bi + CO<sub>2</sub> + Cl<sub>2</sub> [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 46" title="H. Xie, M. Hong, E.M. Hitz, X.Z. Wang, M.J. Cui et al., High-temperature pulse method for nanoparticle redispersion. J. Am. Chem. Soc. 142, 17364–17371 (2020). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1021/jacs.0c04887
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR46" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e719">46</a>]. In order to optimize the synthesis condition, Bi/CNRs-5, Bi/CNRs-30 and Bi/CNRs-TFA were also prepared. All synthesis details are offered in the Experimental Section.</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-1" data-title="Fig.&nbsp;1"><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig1" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Fig.&nbsp;1</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9/figures/1" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp" Schematic illustration of the synthesis route of Bi/CNRs-15. <b>b</b> SEM image of Bi/CNRs-15. <b>c</b> TEM image of Bi/CNRs-15. <b>d</b> HRTEM image of Bi/CNRs-15. <b>e</b> XRD patterns of Bi/CNRs-5, Bi/CNRs-15 and Bi/CNRs-30. <b>f</b> Raman spectrum of Bi/CNRs-15. <b>g</b> EPR spectrum of Bi/CNRs-15</p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9/figures/1" data-track-dest="link:Figure1 Full size image" aria-label="Full size image figure 1" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" focusable="false" role="img" aria-hidden="true" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#icon-eds-i-chevron-right-small"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><p>Figures S3 and 1b, c present the field-emission scanning electron microscopy (FESEM) and transmission electron microscopy (TEM) images of Bi/CNRs-15, respectively. Clearly, Bi nanoparticles with an average particle size of 26.5&nbsp;nm (Fig. S4) are homogeneously loaded in the carbon nanorods, which profits from the rapid cooling/heating rate. In sharp contrast, the analogs of Bi/CNRs-TFA synthesized through a TFA method display aggregated particles, nonuniform size distribution and low metal loading (Figs. S5 and S6), which are principally caused by prolonged heat treatment and slow cooling/heating rate. The samples with different pulse time (5 and 30&nbsp;s) are also presented in Fig. S7. It is evident that Bi/CNRs-15 exhibits the best dispersity in these three samples. Figure&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#Fig1">1</a>d shows the high-resolution TEM (HRTEM) image of Bi/CNRs-15, where highly crystallized nanoparticles can be observed with interlayer distances of 0.326 and 0.234&nbsp;nm, corresponding to (012) and (104) planes of metallic Bi. The XRD patterns of Bi/CNRs-5, Bi/CNRs-15, Bi/CNRs-30, and Bi/CNRs-TFA are shown in Figs. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#Fig1">1</a>e and S8, respectively. With increasing the thermal shock time, the XRD peaks assigned to BiOCl (JCPDS No. 06-0249) disappear until 15&nbsp;s and the present sharp peaks are indexed to the high-crystallinity rhombohedral Bi phase (JCPDS No. 85-1329). Note that the average crystallite size of the Bi particles calculated from Scherrer equation (Table <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="supplementary material anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#MOESM1">S1</a>) is larger than that observed from TEM (26.5&nbsp;nm). The possible reason is that XRD gives volume-weighted measurements, which tends to overestimate the geometric particle size [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="T. Li, A.J. Senesi, B. Lee, Small angle X-ray scattering for nanoparticle research. Chem. Rev. 116, 11128–11180 (2016). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1021/acs.chemrev.5b00690
                  
                " href="#ref-CR47" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e775">47</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="M.M. Modena, B. Rühle, T.P. Burg, S. Wuttke, Nanoparticle characterization: what to measure? Adv. Mater. 31, 1901556 (2019). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/adma.201901556
                  
                " href="#ref-CR48" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e775_1">48</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 49" title="C. Li, Y.R. Pei, M. Zhao, C.C. Yang, Q. Jiang, Sodium storage performance of ultrasmall SnSb nanoparticles. Chem. Eng. J. 420, 129617 (2021). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.cej.2021.129617
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR49" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e778">49</a>]. Moreover, the well-defined crystallinity of Bi/CNRs-15 can be identified by the selected area electron diffraction (SAED) pattern in Fig. S9. A series of clear spotty diffraction rings portray the polycrystallinity of Bi/CNRs-15, further validating the XRD result [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 50" title="R. Serra-Maia, P. Kumar, A.C. Meng, A.C. Foucher, Y. Kang et al., Nanoscale chemical and structural analysis during in situ scanning/transmission electron microscopy in liquids. ACS Nano 15, 10228–10240 (2021). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1021/acsnano.1c02340
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR50" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e782">50</a>]. As shown in Fig. S10, the bright-field scanning transmission electron microscopy (BF-STEM) and corresponding energy-dispersive spectrum (EDS) mapping images unambiguously reveal that Bi and C elements are homogeneously distributed in the Bi/CNRs-15 composite without obvious aggregation.</p><p>XPS was measured to investigate the surface characteristics of the Bi/CNRs-15 hybrid, where only C, Bi, and O elements are perceived (Fig. S11). The high-resolution C 1<i>s</i> spectrum (Fig. S12) can be deconvoluted into three peaks at 284.8, 285.7, and 289.2&nbsp;eV, being ascribed to C–C/C=C, C–O, and C=O bonds, respectively [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 51" title="W.T. Jing, Y. Zhang, Y. Gu, Y.F. Zhu, C.C. Yang et al., N-doped carbon nanonecklaces with encapsulated Sb as a sodium-ion battery anode. Matter 1, 720–733 (2019). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.matt.2019.03.010
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR51" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e791">51</a>]. Two pairs of peaks shown in the Bi 4f high-resolution XPS spectrum (Fig. S13) are assigned to metallic Bi (157.3 and 162.7&nbsp;eV) and Bi<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> (159.2 and 164.6&nbsp;eV), resulting from unavoidable oxidation of highly active Bi in the nanoscale under ambient air [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 22" title="R.C. Cui, H.Y. Zhou, J.C. Li, C.C. Yang, Q. Jiang, Ball-Cactus-like Bi embedded in N-riched carbon nanonetworks enables the best potassium storage performance. Adv. Funct. Mater. 31, 2103067 (2021). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/adfm.202103067
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR22" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e798">22</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 27" title="L. Liu, S. Li, L. Hu, X. Liang, W. Yang et al., Bi@C nanosphere anode with Na+-ether-solvent cointercalation behavior to achieve fast sodium storage under extreme low temperatures. Carbon Energy 6, e531 (2024). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/cey2.531
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR27" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e802">27</a>]. After etching 10&nbsp;nm, the peak intensity of Bi<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> (Fig. S13b) is obviously much weaker than that without etching, proving that Bi<sub>2</sub>O<sub>3</sub> mainly exists on the surface of the sample. The high-resolution O 1<i>s</i> spectrum (Fig. S14) can be fitted into three peaks with the binding energy of 530.3, 532.4, and 533.9&nbsp;eV, corresponding to Bi–O, C–O–Bi, and C–O bonds, respectively. The C–O–Bi bond is a chemical bond formed between C and O atoms, and the O atom also interacts with Bi, which involves the coordination of organic ligands to metal ion centers [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 44" title="D. Yao, C. Tang, L. Li, B. Xia, A. Vasileff et al., In situ fragmented bismuth nanoparticles for electrocatalytic nitrogen reduction. Adv. Energy Mater. 10, 2001289 (2020). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/aenm.202001289
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR44" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e817">44</a>]. As observed in the Raman spectrum (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#Fig1">1</a>f), there are two typical peaks located at 1340 and 1596&nbsp;cm<sup>−1</sup>, attributing to D bands (defective structure) and G bands (graphite structure) of carbonous materials, respectively. Moreover, the D band can be further deconvoluted into three peaks at 1345 (D1), 1183 (D2), and 1497 (D3) cm<sup>−1</sup>, respectively. The D1 band corresponds to the disorders and defects in carbon lattice and the D2 band is ascribed to edge defects, while the D3 band is associated with amorphous <i>sp</i><sup>3</sup> carbon [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Q. Lai, J. Zheng, Z. Tang, D. Bi, J. Zhao et al., Optimal configuration of N-doped carbon defects in 2D turbostratic carbon nanomesh for advanced oxygen reduction electrocatalysis. Angew. Chem. Int. Ed. 59, 11999–12006 (2020). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/anie.202000936
                  
                " href="#ref-CR52" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e832">52</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="J. Wang, Y. Yao, C. Zhang, Q. Sun, D. Cheng et al., Superstructured macroporous carbon rods composed of defective graphitic nanosheets for efficient oxygen reduction reaction. Adv. Sci. 8, e2100120 (2021). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/advs.202100120
                  
                " href="#ref-CR53" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e832_1">53</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 54" title="Y. Chen, B. Xi, M. Huang, L. Shi, S. Huang et al., Defect-selectivity and “order-in-disorder” engineering in carbon for durable and fast potassium storage. Adv. Mater. 34, e2108621 (2022). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/adma.202108621
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR54" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e835">54</a>]. The calculated ratios of <i>I</i><sub>D1</sub>/<i>I</i><sub>G</sub> based on integrated peak intensity is 1.86, disclosing abundant defects and disorders in Bi/CNRs-15. To further corroborate defects in Bi/CNRs-15, electron paramagnetic resonance (EPR) characterization was also carried out. As presented in Figs. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#Fig1">1</a>g and S15, the strong EPR signal at <i>g</i> = 2.0034 is associated with the rich carbon vacancies in the Bi/CNRs-15 hybrid [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 53" title="J. Wang, Y. Yao, C. Zhang, Q. Sun, D. Cheng et al., Superstructured macroporous carbon rods composed of defective graphitic nanosheets for efficient oxygen reduction reaction. Adv. Sci. 8, e2100120 (2021). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/advs.202100120
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR53" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e853">53</a>], which is well consistent with the Raman spectrum. Compared to Bi/CNRs-TFA, the continuous gas emission can sacrifice irreversible heteroatom defects while induce more reversible carbon vacancies under extreme heating conditions derived from HTS [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 54" title="Y. Chen, B. Xi, M. Huang, L. Shi, S. Huang et al., Defect-selectivity and “order-in-disorder” engineering in carbon for durable and fast potassium storage. Adv. Mater. 34, e2108621 (2022). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/adma.202108621
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR54" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e856">54</a>]. These abundant vacancies are able to furnish more active sites for the absorption and diffusion of Na<sup>+</sup>, which is beneficial for Na storage [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 55" title="Y.R. Pei, H.Y. Zhou, M. Zhao, J.C. Li, X. Ge et al., High-efficiency sodium storage of Co0.85Se/WSe2 encapsulated in N-doped carbon polyhedron via vacancy and heterojunction engineering. Carbon Energy 6, 374 (2024). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/cey2.374
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR55" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e861">55</a>]. The Bi content in Bi/CNRs-15 is determined by the TGA in air, which is calculated to be 86.8% from the equation in Fig. S16. To further study the specific surface area and pore texture type of Bi-MOFs and Bi/CNRs-15, nitrogen adsorption–desorption technique was implemented. As shown in Fig. S17, Bi/CNRs-15 displays a typical mesoporous structure with a specific surface area of 48.1 m<sup>2</sup>&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. The high porosity increases the contact areas between the electrolyte and electrode, and decreases the Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion distance, facilitating the rate performance of Bi/CNRs-15 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 56" title="X. Yin, Z. Lu, J. Wang, X. Feng, S. Roy et al., Enabling fast Na+ transfer kinetics in the whole-voltage-region of hard-carbon anodes for ultrahigh-rate sodium storage. Adv. Mater. 34, e2109282 (2022). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/adma.202109282
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR56" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e871">56</a>].</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec10"><span class="c-article-section__title-number">3.2 </span>Low-Temperature Performance</h3><p>The Na storage properties of Bi/CNRs-15 were investigated in 2025 coin-type half cell and full cell at room temperature, which shows remarkable high-rate performance and appealing cycling stability even under high mass loadings (Figs. S18-S27, detailed description in Supporting Information). Based on the well-tailored Bi/CNRs-15 electrode, half cells were also assembled with metallic Na to evaluate the electrochemical performance at low temperature. As shown in Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#Fig2">2</a>a, the Bi/CNRs-15 electrode exhibits admirable adaptability for temperature. The capacity of Bi/CNRs-15 testing at 1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> slightly decreases as the temperature drops to − 40&nbsp;°C, and the capacity can be retrieved and maintain stability when the temperature returns to 0&nbsp;°C. The discharge/charge curves (Fig. S29) display polarized plateaus below − 20&nbsp;°C due to rapidly increasing internal resistance. The CV curves (Fig. S30) under low-temperature conditions show great repetition between the first and second cycles, indicating excellent cycling stability and Na<sup>+</sup> storage reversibility of the Bi/CNRs-15 electrode. From Fig. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#Fig2">2</a>b–d and S31, the Bi/CNRs-15 electrode represents ultrahigh rate capability (261.4&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>) and superior cycling performance (240.3&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 2400 cycles with a capacity retention of 67.3%) at − 40&nbsp;°C, while Bi/CNRs-TFA only exhibits moderate rate property (101.5&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>). In sharp contrast, the pure Bi electrode is unstable and displays battery invalidity after only several cycles at 1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at − 40&nbsp;°C (Fig. S32). As presented in Figs. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#Fig2">2</a>e and S33, even at − 60&nbsp;°C, Bi/CNRs-15 still displays incredible rate property (237.9&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 2&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>), which is much better than other anode materials previously reported in open literatures (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#Fig2">2</a>f and Table S2). Simultaneously, Bi/CNRs-15 also exhibits competitive cycling stability (237.1&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 150 cycles) [Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#Fig2">2</a>g]. Surprisingly, the phenomenon of exceeding theoretical capacity appears in Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#Fig2">2</a>b, which has been reported for different kinds of electrode materials (carbon, metal, metal oxide, metal sulfides, etc.) [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="H. Long, J. Wang, S. Zhao, B. Zou, L. Yan et al., Enable the domino-like structural recovering in bismuth anode to achieve fast and durable Na/K storages. Angew. Chem. Int. Ed. 63, e202406513 (2024). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/anie.202406513
                  
                " href="#ref-CR57" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e929">57</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" title="Q. Li, H. Li, Q. Xia, Z. Hu, Y. Zhu et al., Extra storage capacity in transition metal oxide lithium-ion batteries revealed by in situ magnetometry. Nat. Mater. 20, 76–83 (2021). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1038/s41563-020-0756-y
                  
                " href="#ref-CR58" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e929_1">58</a>,<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 59" title="Z.-S. Wu, G. Zhou, L.-C. Yin, W. Ren, F. Li et al., Graphene/metal oxide composite electrode materials for energy storage. Nano Energy 1, 107–131 (2012). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.nanoen.2011.11.001
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR59" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e932">59</a>]. In this work, the extra capacity may come from interfacial charge storage [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 58" title="Q. Li, H. Li, Q. Xia, Z. Hu, Y. Zhu et al., Extra storage capacity in transition metal oxide lithium-ion batteries revealed by in situ magnetometry. Nat. Mater. 20, 76–83 (2021). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1038/s41563-020-0756-y
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR58" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e935">58</a>]. Additionally, carbonaceous materials can store extra Na in pores and cavities [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 59" title="Z.-S. Wu, G. Zhou, L.-C. Yin, W. Ren, F. Li et al., Graphene/metal oxide composite electrode materials for energy storage. Nano Energy 1, 107–131 (2012). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.nanoen.2011.11.001
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR59" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e938">59</a>].</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-2" data-title="Fig.&nbsp;2"><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig2" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Fig.&nbsp;2</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9/figures/2" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp" height="513"></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="figure-2-desc"><p>Half-cell performance at ultralow temperature. <b>a</b> Cycling performance of Bi/CNRs-15 at 1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at different temperatures. <b>b</b> Rate performance of Bi/CNRs-15 at − 40&nbsp;°C. <b>c</b> Charge/discharge curves of Bi/CNRs-15 at various rates at − 40&nbsp;°C. <b>d</b> Long-term cycling performance of Bi/CNRs-15 at 1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at − 40&nbsp;°C. <b>e</b> Rate performance of Bi/CNRs-15 at − 60&nbsp;°C. <b>f</b> Comparisons of rate performance with reported low-temperature SIB anodes. <b>g</b> Cycling performance of Bi/CNRs-15 at 1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at − 60&nbsp;°C</p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9/figures/2" data-track-dest="link:Figure2 Full size image" aria-label="Full size image figure 2" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" focusable="false" role="img" aria-hidden="true" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#icon-eds-i-chevron-right-small"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><p>To preliminarily estimate the practical applications of the Bi/CNRs-15 hybrid in extremely cold areas, the full cell was fabricated using Bi/CNRs-15 as an anode, and NVP as a cathode with a negative/positive (N/P) ratio of 1.01 (see Supporting Information for details) for the electrochemical performance test (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#Fig3">3</a>a). The Bi/CNRs-15//NVP full cell exhibits excellent fast charging capability at − 40&nbsp;°C with a high capacity of 382.9&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> (based on active mass of the anode), in which 58.9% of the capacity can be retained even when the current density increases by 20-folds from 0.1 to 2 A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> (Figs. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#Fig3">3</a>b and S34). Note that the specific capacity of the full cell is lower than that of the half cell owing to the un-optimized cathode and the problem of matching the anode and cathode [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 60" title="L. Jing, K. Zhuo, L. Sun, N. Zhang, X. Su et al., The mass-balancing between positive and negative electrodes for optimizing energy density of supercapacitors. J. Am. Chem. Soc. 146, 14369–14385 (2024). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1021/jacs.4c00486
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR60" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e1004">60</a>]. As illustrated in Fig. S35, the full cell displays appealing cycling stability (a capacity retention of 97.0% at 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after 100 cycles) after high-rate cycling. As shown in Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#Fig3">3</a>c, the full cell presents a stable capacity retention of 63.9% at 1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> over 1000 cycles. It should be noted that the charged full cell can power the light-emitting diodes (LEDs) at − 40&nbsp;°C (Figs. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#Fig3">3</a>d and S36). The practical feasibility is further evaluated by the pouch cell (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#Fig3">3</a>e), which displays 75.8% capacity retention after 100 cycles at 1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. It should be noted that the coulombic efficiencies of the Bi/CNR-15//NVP pouch cell are lower than 100%, which is caused by the NVP cathode with relatively low CEs of 98.8% and the un-optimized N/P ratio [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 61" title="H. Zhang, S. Zhang, B. Guo, L.-J. Yu, L. Ma et al., MoS2 hollow multishelled nanospheres doped Fe single atoms capable of fast phase transformation for fast-charging Na-ion batteries. Angew. Chem. Int. Ed. 63, e202400285 (2024). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/anie.202400285
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR61" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e1023">61</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 62" title="H. Zhang, L. Wang, L. Ma, Y. Liu, B. Hou et al., Surface crystal modification of Na3V2(PO4)3 to cast intermediate Na2V2(PO4)3 phase toward high-rate sodium storage. Adv. Sci. 11, e2306168 (2024). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/advs.202306168
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR62" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e1026">62</a>]. Figure&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#Fig3">3</a>f demonstrates that the assembled full cell delivers a high energy density of 181.9&nbsp;Wh&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup> at a power density of 45.5&nbsp;W&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup>, and even 37.9&nbsp;Wh&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup> at a power density of 1119.5&nbsp;W&nbsp;kg<sup>−1</sup> (based on the total mass of the cathode and anode). Even at − 60&nbsp;°C, the full cell still delivers a capacity of 190.4&nbsp;mAh&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> at 1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> (Figs. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#Fig3">3</a>g and S37). Totally, the achieved performances illustrate that the as-fabricated Bi/CNRs-15//NVP system possesses outstanding temperature adaptability, fast charging capability, and ultralong lifespan at ultralow temperature, providing evidences of Bi/CNRs-15 as a feasible anode for practical applications in low-temperature SIBs.</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-3" data-title="Fig.&nbsp;3"><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig3" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Fig.&nbsp;3</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9/figures/3" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp" height="503"></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="figure-3-desc"><p>Full-cell performance at ultralow temperature. <b>a</b> The schematic diagram of the full cell with the Bi/CNRs-15 anode and NVP cathode (Bi/CNRs-15//NVP). <b>b</b> Rate performance of the Bi/CNRs-15//NVP full cell at − 40&nbsp;°C. <b>c</b> Long-term cycling
