data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9/figures/3" data-track-dest="link:Figure3 Full size image" aria-label="Full size image figure 3" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" focusable="false" role="img" aria-hidden="true" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#icon-eds-i-chevron-right-small"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec11"><span class="c-article-section__title-number">3.3 </span>Charge Storage Kinetics</h3><p>The detailed Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion kinetics of Bi/CNRs-15 and pure Bi were assessed by the galvanostatic intermittent titration technique (GITT) at both 25 and − 40&nbsp;°C. Clearly, the slope region possesses higher Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficient (<i>D</i>) due to fast Na<sup>+</sup> adsorption on the surface [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 63" title="X. Yi, X. Li, J. Zhong, S. Wang, Z. Wang et al., Unraveling the mechanism of different kinetics performance between ether and carbonate ester electrolytes in hard carbon electrode. Adv. Funct. Mater. 32, 2209523 (2022). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/adfm.202209523
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR63" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e1109">63</a>], while the plateau region exhibits lower <i>D</i> because of sluggish alloying/dealloying reactions. As the temperature drops to − 40&nbsp;°C, the <i>D</i> values of Bi/CNRs-15 and pure Bi are in ranges of 1.4 × 10<sup>–8</sup> to 7.4 × 10<sup>–13</sup> and 1.4 × 10<sup>–8</sup> to 3.7 × 10<sup>–14</sup>, respectively (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#Fig4">4</a>a-c). In comparison with pure Bi, the enhanced <i>D</i> values of Bi/CNRs-15 under room temperature (Fig. S41) and low temperature, especially in the plateau region, are well consistent with unprecedented rate capability and also support the positive effect of nanoparticles driven by HTS on the kinetics of Na storage. Moreover, the Bi/CNRs-15 anode presents smaller Δ<i>Eτ</i> (instantaneous potential change during the constant current pulse) and Δ<i>E</i>s (steady-state potential change by the current pulse) than the pure Bi anode (Fig. S42), which indicates better Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion ability of Bi/CNRs-15 than pure Bi.</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-4" data-title="Fig.&nbsp;4"><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig4" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Fig.&nbsp;4</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9/figures/4" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp" srcset="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1007%2Fs40820-024-01560-9/MediaObjects/40820_2024_1560_Fig4_HTML.png?as=webp"><img aria-describedby="Fig4" src="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1007%2Fs40820-024-01560-9/MediaObjects/40820_2024_1560_Fig4_HTML.png" alt="figure 4" loading="lazy" width="685" height="537"></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="figure-4-desc"><p>Electrochemical kinetics analysis at various temperatures. <b>a</b> GITT voltage profiles of the Bi/CNRs-15 and pure Bi electrodes at − 40&nbsp;°C. Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficients of Bi/CNRs-15 and pure Bi during the <b>b</b> discharging and <b>c</b> charging processes at − 40&nbsp;°C. <b>d</b> EIS plots of the fresh Bi/CNRs-15 and pure Bi electrodes at 25 and − 40&nbsp;°C, where the inset shows corresponding equivalent circuit diagram and magnified view corresponding to the black box. <b>e</b> Comparisons of <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> and <i>R</i><sub>el</sub> of the Bi/CNRs-15 and pure Bi electrodes at 25 (left) and − 40&nbsp;°C (right). Temperature-dependent EIS study of<b> f</b> Bi/CNRs-15 and <b>g</b> pure Bi from − 40 to 0&nbsp;°C. <b>h</b> Comparisons of <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> of Bi/CNRs-15 and pure Bi at various temperatures. <b>i</b> Arrhenius curves and calculated <i>E</i><sub>a</sub> of Bi/CNRs-15 and pure Bi</p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9/figures/4" data-track-dest="link:Figure4 Full size image" aria-label="Full size image figure 4" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" focusable="false" role="img" aria-hidden="true" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#icon-eds-i-chevron-right-small"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><p>Electrochemical impedance spectroscopy (EIS) measurements were conducted to quantitatively identify the charge transfer resistances and deeply comprehend the superior reaction kinetics of Bi/CNRs-15 [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 64" title="M. Yousaf, Y. Wang, Y. Chen, Z. Wang, A. Firdous et al., A 3D trilayered CNT/MoSe2/C heterostructure with an expanded MoSe2 interlayer spacing for an efficient sodium storage. Adv. Energy Mater. 9, 1900567 (2022). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/aenm.201900567
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR64" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e1210">64</a>]. One semicircle in high and middle frequencies and a straight line in low frequency can be observed in the Nyquist plots of Bi/CNRs-15 and pure Bi, implying similitude electrochemical processes in these two electrodes. The fitting results of charge transfer resistance (<i>R</i><sub>ct</sub>) and electrolyte resistance (<i>R</i><sub>el</sub>) values are quantified with the equivalent circuit. The <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> value decreases gradually with increasing cycles and reaches an extremely low value of 1.2&nbsp;Ω after 50 cycles (Fig. S43), suggesting that the Bi/CNR-15 electrode has excellent stability and maintains high electrochemical reaction kinetics. As presented in Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#Fig4">4</a>d, compared with room temperature, the steep rise of <i>R</i><sub>el</sub> at − 40&nbsp;°C demonstrates low ionic conductivity caused by increased viscosity of the electrolyte [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 65" title="J. Holoubek, H. Liu, Z. Wu, Y. Yin, X. Xing et al., Tailoring electrolyte solvation for Li metal batteries cycled at ultra-low temperature. Nat. Energy 6, 303–313 (2022). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1038/s41560-021-00783-z
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR65" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e1233">65</a>]. We can also find that <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> of Bi/CNRs-15 is slightly lower than that of pure Bi at 25&nbsp;°C while much lower at − 40&nbsp;°C, which indicates that Bi/CNRs-15 has a distinct advantage particularly under low-temperature conditions (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#Fig4">4</a>e). The temperature-dependent EIS was further carried out to measure the values of <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> from − 40 to 0&nbsp;°C (Figs. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#Fig4">4</a>f-h and S45). Based on the Arrhenius equation [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 65" title="J. Holoubek, H. Liu, Z. Wu, Y. Yin, X. Xing et al., Tailoring electrolyte solvation for Li metal batteries cycled at ultra-low temperature. Nat. Energy 6, 303–313 (2022). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1038/s41560-021-00783-z
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR65" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e1251">65</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 66" title="Y.-S. Hu, Y. Lu, The mystery of electrolyte concentration: from superhigh to ultralow. ACS Energy Lett. 5, 3633–3636 (2020). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1021/acsenergylett.0c02234
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR66" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e1254">66</a>],</p><div id="Equ1" class="c-article-equation"><div class="c-article-equation__content"><span class="mathjax-tex">$$T/R_{{{\text{ct}}}} = {\text{ A}}\,{\text{exp}}\left( { - E_{{\text{a}}} /{\text{R}}T} \right)$$</span></div><div class="c-article-equation__number">
                    (1)
                </div></div><p>where <i>T</i> is the temperature, A is a constant and R is the gas constant. The activation energy (<i>E</i><sub>a</sub>) for charge transfer (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#Fig4">4</a>i) of Bi/CNRs-15 is calculated to be 48.2&nbsp;kJ&nbsp;mol<sup>−1</sup>, which is lower than that of pure Bi (50.4&nbsp;kJ&nbsp;mol<sup>−1</sup>). The above results verify that nanomanufacturing and hierarchical porous structure are more conducive to reducing the charge transfer barrier and achieving fast reaction kinetics, which are vital to acquire incredible fast charging capability at extremely low temperature.</p><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec12"><span class="c-article-section__title-number">3.4 </span>Stable SEI Component</h3><p>As an inert layer formed from chemical and electrochemical reactions of components in the electrolyte, SEI plays a critical role in determining the performance of batteries [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 67" title="W. Bai, H. Wang, D.H. Min, J. Miao, B. Li et al., 3D-printed hierarchically microgrid frameworks of sodiophilic Co3O4@C/rGO nanosheets for ultralong cyclic sodium metal batteries. Adv. Sci. 11, e2404419 (2024). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/advs.202404419
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR67" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e1348">67</a>]. Meanwhile, a cold condition can convert the reaction of electrolyte decomposition and results in the formation of metastable SEI with dominant organics, which greatly decelerates the migration of Na<sup>+</sup> [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 68" title="S. Weng, X. Zhang, G. Yang, S. Zhang, B. Ma et al., Temperature-dependent interphase formation and Li+ transport in lithium metal batteries. Nat. Commun. 14, 4474 (2023). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1038/s41467-023-40221-0
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR68" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e1353">68</a>]. In order to further study the relationship between SEI and Na storage behavior, TEM and XPS measurements with different etching depths were carried out for both Bi/CNRs-15 and pure Bi electrodes after 5 cycles at − 40&nbsp;°C. As shown in Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#Fig5">5</a>a, d, the SEI layer of Bi/CNRs-15 is thin (the thickness of 8–20&nbsp;nm) and homogeneous, whereas that of pure Bi is thicker (the thickness of 10–42&nbsp;nm) and uneven. By deeply analyzing the high-resolution spectra of C 1<i>s</i>, F 1<i>s</i>, and O 1<i>s</i> (Figs. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#Fig5">5</a>b, c, e, f and S46), the C 1<i>s</i> peaks at 284.8&nbsp;eV (C–C/C–H), 285.7&nbsp;eV (C–O), 287.1&nbsp;eV (C=O), and O 1<i>s</i> peaks located at 533.2&nbsp;eV (C=O) are associated with organic compounds primarily derived from the decomposition of solvents [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 69" title="M. Liu, F. Wu, Y. Gong, Y. Li, Y. Li et al., Interfacial-catalysis-enabled layered and inorganic-rich SEI on hard carbon anodes in ester electrolytes for sodium-ion batteries. Adv. Mater. 35, e2300002 (2023). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/adma.202300002
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR69" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e1378">69</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 70" title="G. Yan, K. Reeves, D. Foix, Z. Li, C. Cometto et al., A new electrolyte formulation for securing high temperature cycling and storage performances of Na-ion batteries. Adv. Energy Mater. 9, 1901431 (2019). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/aenm.201901431
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR70" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e1382">70</a>]. The peaks at 289.1&nbsp;eV (Na<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub>) of C 1<i>s</i> spectra, the peaks located at 529.7&nbsp;eV (Na<sub>2</sub>O) of O 1<i>s</i> spectra and the peaks at 684.1&nbsp;eV (Na-F) are assigned to inorganic components produced from Na<sup>+</sup>-solvent-PF<sub>6</sub><sup>−</sup> reduction products and the decomposition of NaPF<sub>6</sub> [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 71" title="P.M.L. Le, T.D. Vo, H. Pan, Y. Jin, Y. He et al., Excellent cycling stability of sodium anode enabled by a stable solid electrolyte interphase formed in ether-based electrolytes. Adv. Funct. Mater. 30, 2001151 (2020). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/adfm.202001151
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR71" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e1405">71</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 72" title="H.S. Hirsh, B. Sayahpour, A. Shen, W. Li, B. Lu et al., Role of electrolyte in stabilizing hard carbon as an anode for rechargeable sodium-ion batteries with long cycle life. Energy Storage Mater. 42, 78–87 (2021). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.ensm.2021.07.021
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR72" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e1408">72</a>]. The peaks at 290.6&nbsp;eV (C-F) of C 1<i>s</i> spectra and the peaks located at 689.1&nbsp;eV (C-F) of F 1<i>s</i> spectra illustrate that fluorinated organic compounds reside in SEI layer [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 73" title="L. Zhou, Z. Cao, J. Zhang, Q. Sun, Y. Wu et al., Engineering sodium-ion solvation structure to stabilize sodium anodes: universal strategy for fast-charging and safer sodium-ion batteries. Nano Lett. 20, 3247–3254 (2020). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1021/acs.nanolett.9b05355
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR73" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e1418">73</a>]. A small amount of robust fluorinated organic compounds are highly efficacious to preclude the continuous side reactions of SEI components [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 74" title="J. Zhang, D.-W. Wang, W. Lv, S. Zhang, Q. Liang et al., Achieving superb sodium storage performance on carbon anodes through an ether-derived solid electrolyte interphase. Energy Environ. Sci. 10, 370–376 (2017). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1039/C6EE03367A
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR74" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e1421">74</a>]. As observed in Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#Fig5">5</a>g, h, the concentration of organic species in SEI of pure Bi is commonly higher than that of Bi/CNRs-15, demonstrating more decompositions of solvent existing in the pure Bi electrode. To the extent that the total peak area ratios of Na<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub>, Na<sub>2</sub>O, and Na-F peaks stand for inorganic species in SEI layer. With increasing etching depths, the proportions of inorganic compounds in SEI on the Bi/CNRs-15 electrode gradually step up and are higher than those in SEI of pure Bi throughout. Specifically, NaF with high lowest unoccupied molecular orbital level and decent band gap is a good electron insulator to block electrons [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 75" title="E. Wang, J. Wan, Y.-J. Guo, Q. Zhang, W.-H. He et al., Mitigating electron leakage of solid electrolyte interface for stable sodium-ion batteries. Angew. Chem. Int. Ed. 62, e202216354 (2023). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/anie.202216354
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR75" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e1434">75</a>]. Na<sub>2</sub>CO<sub>3</sub> with relatively high ionic conductivity is conducive to the transport of Na<sup>+</sup> [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 76" title="Q. Zhao, S. Stalin, L.A. Archer, Stabilizing metal battery anodes through the design of solid electrolyte interphases. Joule 5, 1119–1142 (2021). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1016/j.joule.2021.03.024
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR76" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e1444">76</a>]. These two inorganic components can synergize with each other to construct a robust SEI of the anode side. Furthermore, as the sputtering depth increases, the soaring rise in proportion of NaF indicates that the inner SEI layer is mainly composed of inorganic species. The continuous and compact inner SEI layer can effectively buffer the volume expansion and improve the cycling lifetime at low temperature [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 68" title="S. Weng, X. Zhang, G. Yang, S. Zhang, B. Ma et al., Temperature-dependent interphase formation and Li+ transport in lithium metal batteries. Nat. Commun. 14, 4474 (2023). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1038/s41467-023-40221-0
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR68" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e1447">68</a>]. Overall, more inorganic component in SEI layer on the Bi/CNRs-15 electrode greatly interprets the reason for better rate performance and cycling stability of Bi/CNRs-15 than pure Bi.</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-5" data-title="Fig.&nbsp;5"><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig5" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Fig.&nbsp;5</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9/figures/5" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp" srcset="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1007%2Fs40820-024-01560-9/MediaObjects/40820_2024_1560_Fig5_HTML.png?as=webp"><img aria-describedby="Fig5" src="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1007%2Fs40820-024-01560-9/MediaObjects/40820_2024_1560_Fig5_HTML.png" alt="figure 5" loading="lazy" width="685" height="419"></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="figure-5-desc"><p>Surface composition analysis of the Bi/CNRs-15 and pure Bi electrodes operating at − 40&nbsp;°C. <b>a</b> HRTEM image of the Bi/CNRs-15 electrode after 5 cycles at 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. Depth-profiling XPS spectra of <b>b</b> C 1<i>s</i> and<b> c</b> F 1<i>s</i> on the Bi/CNRs-15 electrode. <b>d</b> HRTEM image of the pure Bi electrode after 5 cycles at 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. Depth-profiling XPS spectra of<b> e</b> C 1<i>s</i> and<b> f</b> F 1<i>s</i> on the pure Bi electrode. The proportion of SEI components calculated from <b>g</b> C 1<i>s</i> and <b>h</b> F 1<i>s</i> spectra</p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9/figures/5" data-track-dest="link:Figure5 Full size image" aria-label="Full size image figure 5" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" focusable="false" role="img" aria-hidden="true" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#icon-eds-i-chevron-right-small"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div><h3 class="c-article__sub-heading" id="Sec13"><span class="c-article-section__title-number">3.5 </span>High-Rate Activation</h3><p>Shockingly, we found that the capacity can be restored and even higher at 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after losing almost all capacities at 5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#Fig2">2</a>e). To further explore such an unusual phenomenon named “negative fading”, we tested the cycling performance at 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> after high-rate activation (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#Fig6">6</a>a). Compared with the performance without high-rate activation, Bi/CNRs-15 after high-rate (1/3/5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>) cycling shows capacity increment and stable capacity retention to some extent. The Bi/CNRs-15 electrode with a high mass loading (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#Fig6">6</a>b) also represents better rate property after high-rate activation at − 40&nbsp;°C. As shown in Figs. <a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#Fig6">6</a>c, d, and S47, the electrode activated after high rate of 5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> evolved into smaller-sized coral-like porous nanostructures due to the high mechanical stress during repeated volume changes. To further study the specific surface area of the Bi/CNRs-15 electrode after activation, nitrogen adsorption–desorption test was implemented. It is found that the specific surface area of the Bi/CNRs-15 composite is relatively small (6.8 m<sup>2</sup>&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, Fig. S48) before activation. However, after 5 cycles at 5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, the specific surface area of Bi/CNRs-15 composite increases significantly to 24.7&nbsp;m<sup>2</sup>&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> (Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#Fig6">6</a>e), which is larger than that after 5 cycles at 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> (13.8&nbsp;m<sup>2</sup>&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>, Fig.&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#Fig6">6</a>f). The expanded specific surface area induced by morphology evolution creates additional active sites for interfacial reaction to improve the kinetic properties, resulting in the capacity increment [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 77" title="H. Sun, G. Xin, T. Hu, M. Yu, D. Shao et al., High-rate lithiation-induced reactivation of mesoporous hollow spheres for long-lived lithium-ion batteries. Nat. Commun. 5, 4526 (2014). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1038/ncomms5526
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR77" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e1572">77</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 78" title="H. Kim, W. Choi, J. Yoon, J.H. Um, W. Lee et al., Exploring anomalous charge storage in anode materials for next-generation Li rechargeable batteries. Chem. Rev. 120, 6934–6976 (2020). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1021/acs.chemrev.9b00618
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR78" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e1575">78</a>]. Ulteriorly, the instantaneous surface activation under large current can dramatically reduce the side reaction between the anode and the electrolyte [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 79" title="J. Cao, D. Zhang, X. Zhang, Z. Zeng, J. Qin et al., Strategies of regulating Zn2+ solvation structures for dendrite-free and side reaction-suppressed zinc-ion batteries. Energy Environ. Sci. 15, 499–528 (2022). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1039/D1EE03377H
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR79" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e1578">79</a>]. The EIS tests were also conducted to further understand the nature behind the excellent electrochemical performance of high-rate activation. As shown in Fig. S49, the value of <i>R</i><sub>ct</sub> after 5 cycles at 5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> is only 74.5 Ω, much lower than that after 5 cycles at 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> (174.6 Ω). Figure&nbsp;<a data-track="click" data-track-label="link" data-track-action="figure anchor" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#Fig6">6</a>g-i demonstrates that the SEI layer of the Bi/CNRs-15 electrode after 5 cycles at 5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> (the thickness of 7–14&nbsp;nm) is thinner than that of the Bi/CNRs-15 electrode at 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> (the thickness of 8–20&nbsp;nm). The dense inorganic species dominate in the inner layer, while a small number of organic compounds are distributed near the surface, showing a layered structure. This is beneficial for Na<sup>+</sup> transfer and enhances the rate capability of the Bi/CNRs-15 electrode after high-rate activation [<a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 80" title="R. Dong, L. Zheng, Y. Bai, Q. Ni, Y. Li et al., Elucidating the mechanism of fast Na storage kinetics in ether electrolytes for hard carbon anodes. Adv. Mater. 33, e2008810 (2021). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/adma.202008810
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR80" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e1600">80</a>, <a data-track="click" data-track-action="reference anchor" data-track-label="link" data-test="citation-ref" aria-label="Reference 81" title="Y. Wan, K. Song, W. Chen, C. Qin, X. Zhang et al., Ultra-high initial coulombic efficiency induced by interface engineering enables rapid, stable sodium storage. Angew. Chem. Int. Ed. 60, 11481–11486 (2021). 
                  https://doi.org/10.1002/anie.202102368
                  
                " href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9#ref-CR81" id="ref-link-section-d14698485e1603">81</a>]. Overall, due to thinner and more homogeneous SEI layer after high-rate activation and more active sites induced by morphology evolution for redox reaction, the Bi/CNRs-15 electrode after high-rate activation delivers better sodium storage performance. This unique perspective can be used for obtaining high capacity and superior stability of the Bi-based electrodes at low temperature by creating new electrochemically active sites under large current.</p><div class="c-article-section__figure js-c-reading-companion-figures-item" data-test="figure" data-container-section="figure" id="figure-6" data-title="Fig.&nbsp;6"><figure><figcaption><b id="Fig6" class="c-article-section__figure-caption" data-test="figure-caption-text">Fig.&nbsp;6</b></figcaption><div class="c-article-section__figure-content"><div class="c-article-section__figure-item"><a class="c-article-section__figure-link" data-test="img-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="image" data-track-action="view figure" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9/figures/6" rel="nofollow"><picture><source type="image/webp" srcset="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1007%2Fs40820-024-01560-9/MediaObjects/40820_2024_1560_Fig6_HTML.png?as=webp"><img aria-describedby="Fig6" src="//media.springernature.com/lw685/springer-static/image/art%3A10.1007%2Fs40820-024-01560-9/MediaObjects/40820_2024_1560_Fig6_HTML.png" alt="figure 6" loading="lazy" width="685" height="1055"></picture></a></div><div class="c-article-section__figure-description" data-test="bottom-caption" id="figure-6-desc"><p>High-rate activation. <b>a</b> Capacity comparisons after high-rate activation (cycled at 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> for 5 times, then 0.1/1/3/5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup> for 5 cycles, finally returned to cycling at 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>). <b>b</b> Rate performance of Bi/CNRs-15 with a high mass loading (about 1&nbsp;mg&nbsp;cm<sup>−2</sup>). <b>c</b> SEM image of the Bi/CNRs-15 electrode after 5 cycles at 5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. <b>d</b> SEM image of the Bi/CNRs-15 electrode after 5 cycles at 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. <b>e</b> N<sub>2</sub> adsorption/desorption isotherms of the Bi/CNRs-15 electrode after 5 cycles at 5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. <b>f</b> N<sub>2</sub> adsorption/desorption isotherms of the Bi/CNRs-15 electrode after 5 cycles at 0.1&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. <b>g</b> HRTEM image of the Bi/CNRs-15 electrode after 5 cycles at 5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup>. Depth-profiling XPS spectra of <b>h</b> C 1<i>s</i> and <b>i</b> F 1<i>s</i> on the Bi/CNRs-15 electrode after 5 cycles at 5&nbsp;A&nbsp;g<sup>−1</sup></p></div></div><div class="u-text-right u-hide-print"><a class="c-article__pill-button" data-test="article-link" data-track="click" data-track-label="button" data-track-action="view figure" href="/article/10.1007/s40820-024-01560-9/figures/6" data-track-dest="link:Figure6 Full size image" aria-label="Full size image figure 6" rel="nofollow"><span>Full size image</span><svg width="16" height="16" focusable="false" role="img" aria-hidden="true" class="u-icon"><use xmlns:xlink="http://www.w3.org/1999/xlink" xlink:href="#icon-eds-i-chevron-right-small"></use></svg></a></div></figure></div></div></div></section><section data-title="Conclusions"><div class="c-article-section" id="Sec14-section"><h2 class="c-article-section__title js-section-title js-c-reading-companion-sections-item" id="Sec14"><span class="c-article-section__title-number">4 </span>Conclusions</h2><div class="c-article-section__content" id="Sec14-content"><p>In this work, a Bi/CNRs-15 hybrid has been elaborately constructed through ultrafast HTS method. The unique HTS process with rapid elevating/quenching rates and short heating time in seconds enables the synthesis of well-dispersed and high-loading ultrafine metallic nanoparticles. As revealed, Bi/CNRs-15 not only exhibits high Na<sup>+</sup> diffusion coefficient, but also possesses low charge transfer activation energy. Being used as the anode material for SIBs, Bi/CNRs-15 displays unprecedented fast-charging ability at ultralow temperature. The full cell (Bi/CNRs-15//NVP) also delivers a high energy density and a promising power density at − 40&nbsp;°C. Furthermore, a stable and homogenous SEI layer with more inorganic species could improve the structural stability and boost rate kinetics in some degree, which is unraveled by X-ray photoelectron spectroscopy etching. More importantly, an abnormal phenomenon at low temperature of capacity increment named “negative fading” is explored. The guidance of this work makes it possible for further applications of low-temperature fast-charging SIBs.</p></div></div></section>
                                </div>
